GT Equivalence Verification (MatSci8)

GT: c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) + epsilon**c4*c5*(T - c6)
Candidate formulas: 58

Let  
\[
\text{GT}=23.78834\,\epsilon\big(-0.0504201\,(T-330.2004)+1\big)+5.22950\,\epsilon^{0.9585455}(T-330.2004).
\]

First rewrite GT into a simple “basis” form (collecting coefficients of \(T\) and constants):
- Expand the first term:
\[
23.78834\,\epsilon\left(1-0.0504201\,T+0.0504201\cdot 330.2004\right)
=23.78834\,\epsilon\left((1+0.0504201\cdot 330.2004)-0.0504201\,T\right).
\]
So it is of the form \(A\,\epsilon + B\,T\epsilon\) with fixed nonzero \(B\).
- Second term:
\[
5.22950\,\epsilon^{0.9585455}T - 5.22950\cdot 330.2004\,\epsilon^{0.9585455},
\]
so it is of the form \(C\,T\epsilon^{p}+D\,\epsilon^{p}\) with \(p=0.9585455\neq 1\).

Therefore GT is exactly a sum of **four** independent monomials:
\[
\text{GT} = \alpha\,T\epsilon \;+\; \beta\,\epsilon \;+\; \gamma\,T\epsilon^{p}\;+\;\delta\,\epsilon^{p},
\quad p=0.9585455,
\]
with \(\alpha,\beta,\gamma,\delta\) all nonzero.

So any candidate must be able (by choosing its constants) to produce **both**:
- a \(T\epsilon\) term and an \(\epsilon\) term, and
- a \(T\epsilon^{p}\) term and an \(\epsilon^{p}\) term,
with the **same exponent \(p\)** in both places, and **no extra functional dependence** (no logs, exp(T·), sin, rational in \(\epsilon\), etc.), unless those can be eliminated by setting coefficients to 0.

Now check candidates.

---

### 1
Has terms like \(T\), \(T\epsilon\), \(\epsilon^2\), \(\epsilon^{c4}\), constants, \(\epsilon\), \(\epsilon^{c8}\).  
No way to create \(T\epsilon^{p}\) because \(T\) only appears as \(T\) and \(T\epsilon\), not multiplied by \(\epsilon^{c}\) with free exponent. **No match.**

### 2
\(T c0 \epsilon\) plus only \(\epsilon\)-powers (no \(T\epsilon^{p}\) unless \(p=1\)). GT needs \(T\epsilon^{0.9585}\). **No match.**

### 3
Has \(T\epsilon\) and \(\epsilon^{c}\) terms, plus an exponential \(\epsilon^{c5}\exp(c6/T)\). To match GT we must remove exp term (set \(c4=0\)), but then still no \(T\epsilon^{p}\) term. **No match.**

### 4
Has \(T\) alone, not \(T\epsilon\) unless via exp term (but that’s \( \epsilon^{c8}\exp(Tc9)\)). Cannot form \(T\epsilon\) and \(T\epsilon^{p}\) cleanly. **No match.**

### 5
Only \(T\) alone and \(\epsilon\)-powers; no \(T\epsilon\) or \(T\epsilon^{p}\). **No match.**

### 6
Only \(T\) alone and \(\epsilon\)-powers; no \(T\epsilon^{p}\). **No match.**

### 7
Has \(T\epsilon\) and \(\epsilon^{c}\) terms plus \(\epsilon^{c5}\exp(c6/T)\). If set \(c4=0\) to remove exp, still lacks \(T\epsilon^{p}\). If keep exp, cannot equal linear \((T-330)\) dependence. **No match.**

### 8

### 9

### 10

### 11

### 12

### 13

### 16

### 32

### 33
Has \(T\epsilon\) and also \(T^{c1}\epsilon^{c3}\) plus \(\epsilon\)-powers. Could we set \(c1=1\) to make \(T^{c1}=T\), and set \(c3=p\) to get \(T\epsilon^{p}\). Yes, that yields a \(T\epsilon^{p}\) term.  
But GT also needs a **constant-times \(\epsilon^{p}\)** term (without \(T\)). Candidate 33 has no standalone \(\epsilon^{p}\) term unless one of the other \(\epsilon\)-power terms is set to exponent \(p\). It has \(c4\epsilon^{c5}\) and \(c6\epsilon^{c7}\), so we can set \(c5=p\) and use that for \(\epsilon^{p}\). Good.  
However GT also needs a standalone \(\epsilon\) term (power 1) and a \(T\epsilon\) term. Candidate already has \(T c0\epsilon\) for \(T\epsilon\). For \(\epsilon\), we could set \(c6\epsilon^{c7}\) to be \(\epsilon\) by choosing \(c7=1\), but then we lose \(\epsilon^{p}\) unless we use \(c4\epsilon^{c5}\) for \(\epsilon^{p}\). That’s fine.  
So structurally candidate 33 can represent:
\[
a\,T\epsilon + b\,T\epsilon^{p} + d\,\epsilon^{p} + e\,\epsilon.
\]
